As for whether the importer and exporter could be the same company, this is indeed possible and quite common. In 2023, 43.4% ($2,208.9 billion) of total U.S. goods trade was between related parties [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQHx3XM5sXf_kjMqyR6fGduOd8O3bJVcUcNjsLFPZH1_0JAnE-Fe3K1G09_4RqPT2eVQSQsIjRZsE0tlc4NFsV-bEqW-sstrGFGLLH3Izb4O3_dttkTBZl_KY9qHG53Hmw==) [11, 14]. This includes transactions between U.S. companies and their foreign subsidiaries, and vice versa [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQHwKYnqbw82Zs5Mht3rCEFOriYuY2d09gTRWoo80YmDjNlahJZ4PI1Ft3i667rSWCQWW3k5LL8ufd6AJNUHfEhVdjLkrfW5txCxltPPkSGIwGArAdqSBW-4UiXOkjN-TXphDw5oUAXc-0WTmnDuTz9ZwCtGOa9GE60PSjgWEZ6udyRfhg==) [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFbyqz9mgkZM5LMtI_xy0r4SskVyYek81Z3j6gD5Yuf2ku63c2Iuo18vdlgw65Z1fXVl1SaNmXucBtLhz3qQyiPjMfVKl9SUupi8W7d6isYMYT9xWlSb2l29r06gOL-Wma-9vdDBryKVeAePOVfuQ1YOLMrJIVBEq1VVMkx5JMRZA5q5w==) [3, 11]. Specifically, related-party trade accounted for 49.3% of imports and 34.4% of exports in 2023 [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/grounding-api-redirect/AUZIYQFbyqz9mgkZM5LMtI_xy0r4SskVyYek81Z3j6gD5Yuf2ku63c2Iuo18vdlgw65Z1fXVl1SaNmXucBtLhz3qQyiPjMfVKl9SUupi8W7d6isYMYT9xWlSb2l29r06gOL-Wma-9vdDBryKVeAePOVfuQ1YOLMrJIVBEq1VVMkx5JMRZA5q5w==) [11].

--- Research Result 1 ---
Based on the search results, here's a breakdown of who pays tariffs and related fact checks, particularly concerning claims made by Donald Trump:

**Who Pays Tariffs?**

*   **Importers Generally Pay:** The consensus is that tariffs are typically paid by domestic importers (American companies in the case of US tariffs) to the country's customs authority (e.g., U.S. Customs and Border Protection). [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [3, 4, 7, 9, 10]
*   **Not Foreign Exporters:** Exporters generally do not directly pay the tariff. [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3) [4, 11] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)
*   **Impact on Exporters:** However, tariffs can negatively affect exporters because their products become more expensive in the importing market. [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [oneunionsolutions](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-12) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) This may force them to lower prices, sacrificing profits, or to find alternative markets. [3, 4, 5]

**Trump's Claims vs. Reality** [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-13)

*   **False Claim:** Donald Trump has repeatedly claimed that foreign countries pay tariffs to the U.S. [3, 11] [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7)
*   **The Reality:** This claim is false. [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) It is U.S. importers who pay the tariffs. [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [3, 11] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)
*   **Consumers Bear the Cost:** Economists generally agree that a significant portion of the tariff cost is passed on to domestic consumers through higher prices. [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [3, 9, 10, 13] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)

*   **Tariffs as a Tax:** Tariffs are a tax on imports, usually calculated as a percentage of the price the buyer pays the foreign seller. [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [3, 4, 9, 10]
*   **Effects on Trade:** Tariffs can reduce demand for foreign goods. [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [oneunionsolutions](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-12) [1] They can also lead to retaliatory tariffs from other countries, harming a country's export sector. *   **Economic Consequences:** [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8)
    *   Tariffs can lead to higher prices for businesses and consumers. [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [2] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)
    *   They can distort resource allocation, increase production costs, and cause currency appreciation, which hurts exporters. [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [2] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)

[uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [1] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)

[pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [3] In early 2025, he enacted steep tariffs, raising the average effective U.S. tariff rate significantly. [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-14) [14] [factcheck](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-4) [time](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-2) [europa](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-5) [nortonrosefulbright](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-1) [economictimes](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-0) [treasury](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-6) [rnz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-7) [pbs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-8) [poynter](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-9) [uchicago](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-10) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-11) [instituteforgovernment](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/0-3)

--- Research Result 2 ---
Based on the search results, here's a synthesis of the current situation regarding tariffs paid by exporters and importers within the same company, particularly in light of recent trade developments:

**General Landscape:**

*   **Increased Scrutiny:** Tax and customs authorities are increasingly scrutinizing related-party transactions, including those involving multinational groups and large enterprises. [bovemontero](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) They are using automated risk analysis tools and enhancing international cooperation to prevent tax base erosion. [bovemontero](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0)
*   **Transfer Pricing Impact:** Tariffs are no longer just a trade issue but have significant implications for companies' transfer pricing models. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)
*   **Coordination is Key:** Companies need to coordinate their customs, operational planning, and transfer pricing policies to avoid disputes with taxing authorities. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)
*   **Documentation:** Thorough documentation is crucial to ensure compliance with customs and transfer pricing regulations across various jurisdictions. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3)
*   **Global Baseline Tariff:** A 10% *ad valorem* global baseline tariff on all imported goods was announced on April 2, 2025, and went into effect on April 5, 2025, under the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (IEEPA). [womblebonddickinson](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) This generally applies to countries not covered by specific exemptions or higher rates. [womblebonddickinson](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4)
*   **Reciprocal Tariffs:** The US imposed "reciprocal tariffs" on countries based on trade deficits, with a minimum increase of 10 percentage points. [cepr](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5)
*   **"Liberation Day" Tariffs:** On April 2, 2025, President Trump announced "Liberation Day" tariffs with the aim of addressing trade imbalances and encouraging foreign companies to relocate production to the US. [dentons](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-6)

**Transfer Pricing and Customs Valuation:**

*   **Inverse Relationship:** In related-party sales, tariffs and transfer pricing have an inverse relationship. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) Transfer pricing adjustments that reduce income in one area while increasing it in another will likely attract scrutiny. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)
*   **Arm's Length Principle:** Transfer pricing rules require intercompany transactions to mimic what unrelated parties would do. [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) However, applying this principle is challenging when tariffs are high and changing rapidly. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)
*   **Customs Valuation Review:** Rising customs duties can disrupt transfer pricing arrangements. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) Multinational companies should analyze their supply chains and conduct up-to-date customs valuation reviews. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3)
*   **Potential Conflicts:** Customs authorities require import values to reflect arm's-length pricing and may challenge undervalued related-party transactions. Tax authorities may question profit shifting if there's no operational justification. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) This can lead to a situation where a company pays tariffs on an inflated import value but reports a lower value for tax purposes. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)
*   **Mitigation Strategies:** Companies are exploring strategies to mitigate tariffs, such as the First Sale Rule, which allows importers in multi-tiered transactions to declare the customs value of goods based on the price paid in the first sale. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) However, these efforts are not immune from scrutiny. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)
*   **Transfer Price Adjustments:** Companies may need to renegotiate transfer prices due to increased costs from tariffs, deciding how much of the cost to pass on to customers and how tariff fees will be shared between related entities. [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) These changes should be reflected in updated intercompany agreements. [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7)

**Specific Tariff Measures and Trade Relations (as of June 2025):**

*   **China:** The U.S. maintains a complex tariff structure with China, including Section 301 tariffs, IEEPA tariffs, and tariffs related to fentanyl. [freightwaves](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-8) [maersk](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-9) As of June 18, 2025, the US's average tariff on Chinese goods stood at 51.1 percent, while China's average tariff on American goods was 32.6 percent. [china-briefing](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-10)
*   **Steel and Aluminum:** Tariffs on steel and aluminum remain in place, with the US increasing tariffs on steel and aluminum imports from 25% to 50% effective June 4, 2025. [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-11) [wikipedia](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-12)
*   **Canada and Mexico:** While the USMCA provides exemptions for compliant goods, non-compliant goods are subject to a 25% tariff. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-13) [taxfoundation](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-11) [maersk](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-9)
*   **UK:** The U.S. and UK reached an agreement involving lowered tariffs on British steel, aluminum, and automobiles. [maersk](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-9) [womblebonddickinson](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4)
*   **European Union:** The US will impose a 10% tariff on all imports from the UK (excluding cars, iron and steel which are subject to the higher rates) and a 20% tariff on all imports from the EU and differing rates on imports from other countries.

**Actions for Multinational Companies:**

*   **Re-evaluate Pricing Models:** Rethink pricing models and restructure intercompany agreements. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7)
*   **Quantify Exposure:** Assess tariff exposure product-by-product and entity-by-entity.
*   **Optimize Customs Payments:** Focus on optimizing customs payments by reviewing customs values, HS codes, and countries of origin.
*   **Engage with Regulators:** Communicate with regulators and document strategies. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)
*   **Consider Supply Chain Restructuring:** Changes to supply chains to mitigate tariffs can present risks and trigger tax consequences. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)
*   **Monitor Developments:** Continuously monitor tariff developments and adapt strategies accordingly.

**Important Considerations:**

*   **Economic Impact:** Tariffs are expected to cut revenue growth and profitability for most corporate sectors globally. [fxcintel](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-14)
*   **Cross-Border Payments:** Tariffs can impact cross-border payment flows, potentially reducing payments for goods moving to the US. [fxcintel](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-14)
*   **Legal Challenges:** Some of the tariffs have faced legal challenges, creating uncertainty. For example, the US Court of International Trade ruled in May 2025 that the IEEPA tariffs are illegal, but the decision was stayed pending appeal.
*   **Retaliation:** Trade partners may retaliate with their own tariffs, further complicating the situation. [cepr](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5)

This information is based on the most recent available data as of June 20, 2025, but the trade landscape is constantly evolving, and businesses should stay informed of any new developments.


--- Research Result 3 ---
In 2023, 43.4% ($2,208.9 billion) of total U.S. goods trade ($5,090.6 billion) was between related parties [11, 14]. [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-0) Related-party trade includes transactions between U.S. companies and their foreign subsidiaries, as well as transactions between U.S. subsidiaries of foreign companies and their parent companies [3, 11]. [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-1) [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2)

Here's a breakdown of related-party trade in 2023:

*   **Imports:** Related-party trade accounted for 49.3% ($1,514.1 billion) of imports for consumption ($3,072.5 billion) [11]. [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2)
*   **Exports:** Related-party trade accounted for 34.4% ($694.8 billion) of total exports ($2,018.1 billion) [11]. [census](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-2)

It's worth noting that in 2022, related party trade accounted for 41.3% of total U.S. goods trade [2]. [freightamigo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-3) In 2020, related party trade accounted for 41.8% of total U.S. goods trade and related party imports made up 50.3% of total U.S. imports [5]. [freightamigo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/2-4)


--- Research Result 4 ---
Based on the search results, here are specific strategies, beyond the First Sale Rule, that companies are using to optimize customs payments and minimize tariff liabilities when the importer and exporter are related:

**1. Customs Valuation Planning & Review**

*   **Customs Valuation Review:** Conduct regular reviews of customs valuation to identify red flags and mitigate costs. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) This involves analyzing the customs classification and valuation of goods for optimization purposes. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [weaver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)
*   **Appropriate Methodology:** Ensure the appropriate customs valuation methodology is used and that non-dutiable amounts are excluded to avoid unnecessary tariff payments. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4)
*   **Aligning Customs and Transfer Pricing:** Ensure alignment between customs valuation methods and transfer pricing policies, including the impact of the relationship between related parties, benchmarking timing, and accurate documentation of transfer adjustments reflecting customs regulations. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-6)
*   **Reduce Dutiable Base:** Seek to reduce the dutiable base for customs purposes for intercompany transactions. [internationaltradecomplianceupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7) This can be achieved by excluding non-dutiable elements from the transfer price or, where possible, diverging from the use of transfer pricing for customs purposes and using alternative customs valuation methods. [internationaltradecomplianceupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7)
*   **Strategic Declaration of Transaction Prices:** Declare transaction prices strategically, excluding non-dutiable charges from the customs value. [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) Common non-dutiable charges include fees paid to distributors for exclusive rights or to agents assisting in purchasing goods. [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4)

**2. Transfer Pricing Strategies**

*   **Adjusting Transfer Prices:** Adjust transfer prices between related parties to mitigate the impact of tariffs on profitability, while carefully considering the tax implications. [eisneramper](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-8) [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)
*   **Sharing Tariff Costs:** Share the cost of tariffs between related parties to distribute the financial burden. [eisneramper](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-8)
*   **Transfer Pricing Adjustments:** Manage transfer pricing adjustments carefully, ensuring they are clearly classified and evaluated for tax deductibility under local laws. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)
*   **Documentation:** Maintain thorough documentation to ensure full compliance by multinational companies in various jurisdictions, especially regarding customs and transfer pricing regulations. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)
*   **Benchmarking:** Continuously review benchmarking analyses and adjust transfer pricing policies accordingly, ensuring intercompany agreements consider evolving customs duties and economic functions. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)

**3. [dimerco](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-9) [mossadams](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-10) Supply Chain Optimization & Restructuring**

*   **Supply Chain Mapping:** Develop a clear understanding of the global supply chain, mapping both the physical movement of goods and the legal flow of title passage. [weaver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2)
*   **Restructuring Supply Chains:** Restructure the supply chain, potentially relocating manufacturing operations to mitigate the impact of tariffs. [internationaltradecomplianceupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7)
*   **Review and Optimize Supply Chain Costs:** Conduct a comprehensive review of the supply chain to identify opportunities for cost savings in transportation, insurance, and warehousing. [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-6)
*   **Alternative Sourcing:** Explore alternative sourcing options, either with current suppliers or new ones, incorporating design principles that minimize total costs. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-11)
*   **Renegotiate contracts:** Renegotiate contracts for volumes, supply routes, and managing pricing increases.

**4. Tariff Classification & Country of Origin Planning** [williamsmullen](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-12) [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)

*   **Tariff Classification:** Ensure precise and strategic classification of goods to avoid overpayment and capitalize on favorable tariff treatments. Verify HTS classifications to ensure goods are not erroneously included in a targeted tariff category. [anderinger](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-13)
*   **Country of Origin Planning:** Plan and manage the country of origin for goods strategically to benefit from preferential trade agreements and reduced duty rates. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-11)

**5. Utilizing Special Programs & Provisions**

*   **Free Trade Zones (FTZ):** Utilize FTZs to suspend duties until goods are "exported" out of the zone. [dimerco](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-9)
*   **Duty Drawback:** Utilize duty drawback programs on exported goods for duty recovery. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)

**6. Post-Importation Adjustments**

*   **Post-Importation Price Adjustments:** Consider customs valuation planning related to post-importation price adjustments. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)
*   **Duty Refund Opportunities:** Related parties may use transfer pricing to reflect changed economic conditions, and post-importation adjustments may create duty refund opportunities. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1)

**7. Compliance & Risk Management** [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)

*   **Proactive Risk Management:** Adopt a proactive risk management approach by integrating policies, updating documentation regularly, training staff, and engaging external advisors. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)
*   **Internal Audits:** Conduct internal risk audits to identify potential vulnerabilities before they trigger enforcement. [williamsmullen](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-12)
*   **Compliance Infrastructure:** Establish a designated compliance team and retain outside trade counsel to ensure responsiveness to rapid policy changes. [williamsmullen](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-12)
*   **Voluntary Disclosures:** If errors are discovered, proactively disclose them to CBP to mitigate penalties and demonstrate good faith. [williamsmullen](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-12)

**8. Documentation & Transparency**

*   **Comprehensive Documentation:** Maintain comprehensive documentation (contracts, invoices, Incoterms, proof of payment, and business correspondence) to demonstrate the independence and authenticity of transactions. [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)
*   **Economic Justification:** Evaluate the economic justification of adjustments, determining whether changes are market-driven or reactions to protectionist measures.

**9. Other Strategies**

*   **Lobbying and Advocacy:** Engage in lobbying efforts to advocate for tariff reductions or exclusions.
*   **Digital Transformation:** Embrace digital transformation to optimize input costs and align global trade data and technology with organizational objectives. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-11)
*   **Scenario Planning:** Model various scenarios to understand potential financial impacts, including direct tariff costs, supply chain expenses, currency fluctuation risks, and inventory carrying costs. [globaltrademag](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-14)

These strategies require careful consideration of both customs and tax regulations, as well as thorough documentation to support the chosen approach. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) Companies should also stay informed about evolving trade policies and enforcement trends to adapt their strategies accordingly. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)


--- Research Result 5 ---
Here's a summary of the legal challenges to the IEEPA tariffs and the basis for the US Court of International Trade (CIT) ruling that they are illegal, based on the provided search results:

**Legal Challenges to IEEPA Tariffs:**

*   **Presidential Authority:** The core challenge questions whether the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (IEEPA) grants the President the authority to impose broad tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) Several lawsuits argue that IEEPA does not provide such power, especially the authority to impose sweeping tariffs unilaterally. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3)
*   **Constitutional Grounds:** Some complaints argue that if IEEPA is interpreted to grant the President broad tariff authority, it would be an unconstitutional delegation of powers that are exclusively granted to Congress under the U.S. Constitution (Article I) to regulate trade and impose taxes and duties. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
*   **"Unusual and Extraordinary Threat":** IEEPA requires a declared national emergency based on an "unusual and extraordinary threat" originating substantially outside the U.S. Challenges argue that the tariffs imposed do not "deal with" the specific threats they are purported to address; instead, they create leverage to address those issues. [verfassungsblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7)
*   **Scope of "Regulate":** The government argues that IEEPA's power to "regulate...importation" allows for tariffs. [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [verfassungsblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) However, challengers contend that "regulate" does not equate to unlimited tariff authority to impose sweeping tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
*   **Lack of Congressional Consultation:** Some lawsuits, like the one filed by California, argue that even if IEEPA allows tariffs, it requires the President to consult with Congress before imposing them. [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5)

**Basis for the US Court of International Trade (CIT) Ruling:**

*   **Exceeding Statutory Authority:** The CIT ruled that the IEEPA tariffs exceeded the statutory authority delegated to the President. [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [thomsonreuters](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) The court held that IEEPA does not provide the president with "unbounded authority" to impose unlimited tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)
*   **Constitutional Violation:** The CIT found that the tariffs intruded upon Congress's exclusive constitutional role in regulating trade. [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)
*   **Limited Interpretation of "Regulate":** The CIT reasoned that while IEEPA's reference to the power to "regulate" importation might allow for certain tariffs, it doesn't grant the President unlimited tariff authority to impose sweeping tariffs. [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) The "universal reciprocal tariffs went far beyond the delegation's proper scope." [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
*   **Nexus to the Threat:** The CIT held that the tariffs, such as the border security and fentanyl tariffs, did not "deal with" the specific threats that the Executive Orders purported to address. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) The court determined that merely creating leverage does not meet the statute's "deal with" standard. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10)
*   **Conflict with IEEPA's Intent:** The CIT stated that IEEPA was not intended to grant unfettered power to impose tariffs, and that Section 122 of IEEPA (allowing tariffs to be imposed to respond to balance of payments problems) is the only authorization to impose tariffs pursuant to the statute. [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10)

**Important Considerations:**

*   **Stay Pending Appeal:** It's crucial to note that the Federal Circuit Court of Appeals granted a stay pending appeal, which means the IEEPA tariffs remain in effect while the appeal is considered. [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)
*   **Expedited Review:** The Federal Circuit is set to hear the cases en banc (by the full court) on an expedited basis, suggesting a fast-tracked decision on the merits. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)
*   **Other Legal Authorities:** Even if the IEEPA tariffs are ultimately struck down, the President may attempt to use other legal authorities to impose similar tariffs, though these may come with limitations and potential for further litigation. [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4)
*   **Supreme Court:** Legal challenges to the tariffs may ultimately reach the Supreme Court. [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)
*   **Refunds:** The CIT's ruling declared the IEEPA tariffs illegal for all importers but did not explicitly order the government to issue refunds. [thomsonreuters](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8)

[bovemontero](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0) They are using automated risk analysis tools and enhancing international cooperation to prevent tax base erosion. [bovemontero](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-0)\n*   **Transfer Pricing Impact:** Tariffs are no longer just a trade issue but have significant implications for companies' transfer pricing models. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)\n*   **Documentation:** Thorough documentation is crucial to ensure compliance with customs and transfer pricing regulations across various jurisdictions. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3)\n*   **Global Baseline Tariff:** A 10% *ad valorem* global baseline tariff on all imported goods was announced on April 2, 2025, and went into effect on April 5, 2025, under the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (IEEPA). [womblebonddickinson](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4) This generally applies to countries not covered by specific exemptions or higher rates. [womblebonddickinson](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-4)\n*   **Reciprocal Tariffs:** The US imposed \"reciprocal tariffs\" on countries based on trade deficits, with a minimum increase of 10 percentage points. [cepr](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-5)\n*   **\"Liberation Day\" Tariffs:** On April 2, 2025, President Trump announced \"Liberation Day\" tariffs with the aim of addressing trade imbalances and encouraging foreign companies to relocate production to the US. [dentons](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-6)\n\n**Transfer Pricing and Customs Valuation:**\n\n*   **Inverse Relationship:** In related-party sales, tariffs and transfer pricing have an inverse relationship. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) Transfer pricing adjustments that reduce income in one area while increasing it in another will likely attract scrutiny. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)\n*   **Arm's Length Principle:** Transfer pricing rules require intercompany transactions to mimic what unrelated parties would do. [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) However, applying this principle is challenging when tariffs are high and changing rapidly. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)\n*   **Customs Valuation Review:** Rising customs duties can disrupt transfer pricing arrangements. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3) Multinational companies should analyze their supply chains and conduct up-to-date customs valuation reviews. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-3)\n*   **Potential Conflicts:** Customs authorities require import values to reflect arm's-length pricing and may challenge undervalued related-party transactions. Tax authorities may question profit shifting if there's no operational justification. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1) This can lead to a situation where a company pays tariffs on an inflated import value but reports a lower value for tax purposes. [exactera](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-1)\n*   **Mitigation Strategies:** Companies are exploring strategies to mitigate tariffs, such as the First Sale Rule, which allows importers in multi-tiered transactions to declare the customs value of goods based on the price paid in the first sale. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2) However, these efforts are not immune from scrutiny. [jonesday](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-2)\n*   **Transfer Price Adjustments:** Companies may need to renegotiate transfer prices due to increased costs from tariffs, deciding how much of the cost to pass on to customers and how tariff fees will be shared between related entities. [smith-howard](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/1-7) These changes should be reflected in updated intercompany agreements.     "Based on the search results, here are specific strategies, beyond the First Sale Rule, that companies are using to optimize customs payments and minimize tariff liabilities when the importer and exporter are related:\n\n**1. Customs Valuation Planning & Review**\n\n*   **Customs Valuation Review:** Conduct regular reviews of customs valuation to identify red flags and mitigate costs. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) This involves analyzing the customs classification and valuation of goods for optimization purposes. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [weaver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)\n*   **Appropriate Methodology:** Ensure the appropriate customs valuation methodology is used and that non-dutiable amounts are excluded to avoid unnecessary tariff payments. [kpmg](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4)\n*   **Aligning Customs and Transfer Pricing:** Ensure alignment between customs valuation methods and transfer pricing policies, including the impact of the relationship between related parties, benchmarking timing, and accurate documentation of transfer adjustments reflecting customs regulations. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [diacrongroup](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-6)\n*   **Reduce Dutiable Base:** Seek to reduce the dutiable base for customs purposes for intercompany transactions. [internationaltradecomplianceupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7) This can be achieved by excluding non-dutiable elements from the transfer price or, where possible, diverging from the use of transfer pricing for customs purposes and using alternative customs valuation methods. [internationaltradecomplianceupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7)\n*   **Strategic Declaration of Transaction Prices:** Declare transaction prices strategically, excluding non-dutiable charges from the customs value. [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) Common non-dutiable charges include fees paid to distributors for exclusive rights or to agents assisting in purchasing goods. [claconnect](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4)\n\n**2. Transfer Pricing Strategies**\n\n*   **Adjusting Transfer Prices:** Adjust transfer prices between related parties to mitigate the impact of tariffs on profitability, while carefully considering the tax implications. [eisneramper](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-8) [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)\n*   **Sharing Tariff Costs:** Share the cost of tariffs between related parties to distribute the financial burden. [eisneramper](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-8)\n*   **Transfer Pricing Adjustments:** Manage transfer pricing adjustments carefully, ensuring they are clearly classified and evaluated for tax deductibility under local laws. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)\n*   **Documentation:** Maintain thorough documentation to ensure full compliance by multinational companies in various jurisdictions, especially regarding customs and transfer pricing regulations. [kinstellar](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0)\n*   **Benchmarking:** Continuously review benchmarking analyses and adjust transfer pricing policies accordingly, ensuring intercompany agreements consider evolving customs duties and economic functions. [vatupdate](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)\n\n**3.     "Here's a summary of the legal challenges to the IEEPA tariffs and the basis for the US Court of International Trade (CIT) ruling that they are illegal, based on the provided search results:\n\n**Legal Challenges to IEEPA Tariffs:**\n\n*   **Presidential Authority:** The core challenge questions whether the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (IEEPA) grants the President the authority to impose broad tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) Several lawsuits argue that IEEPA does not provide such power, especially the authority to impose sweeping tariffs unilaterally. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3)\n*   **Constitutional Grounds:** Some complaints argue that if IEEPA is interpreted to grant the President broad tariff authority, it would be an unconstitutional delegation of powers that are exclusively granted to Congress under the U.S. Constitution (Article I) to regulate trade and impose taxes and duties. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)\n*   **\"Unusual and Extraordinary Threat\":** IEEPA requires a declared national emergency based on an \"unusual and extraordinary threat\" originating substantially outside the U.S. Challenges argue that the tariffs imposed do not \"deal with\" the specific threats they are purported to address; instead, they create leverage to address those issues. [verfassungsblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7)\n*   **Scope of \"Regulate\":** The government argues that IEEPA's power to \"regulate...importation\" allows for tariffs. [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1) [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5) [verfassungsblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-7) However, challengers contend that \"regulate\" does not equate to unlimited tariff authority to impose sweeping tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)\n*   **Lack of Congressional Consultation:** Some lawsuits, like the one filed by California, argue that even if IEEPA allows tariffs, it requires the President to consult with Congress before imposing them. [morganlewis](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-5)\n\n**Basis for the US Court of International Trade (CIT) Ruling:**\n\n*   **Exceeding Statutory Authority:** The CIT ruled that the IEEPA tariffs exceeded the statutory authority delegated to the President. [mayerbrown](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-3) [thomsonreuters](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-8) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) The court held that IEEPA does not provide the president with \"unbounded authority\" to impose unlimited tariffs. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)\n*   **Constitutional Violation:** The CIT found that the tariffs intruded upon Congress's exclusive constitutional role in regulating trade. [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)\n*   **Limited Interpretation of \"Regulate\":** The CIT reasoned that while IEEPA's reference to the power to \"regulate\" importation might allow for certain tariffs, it doesn't grant the President unlimited tariff authority to impose sweeping tariffs. [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6) The \"universal reciprocal tariffs went far beyond the delegation's proper scope.\" [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)\n*   **Nexus to the Threat:** The CIT held that the tariffs, such as the border security and fentanyl tariffs, did not \"deal with\" the specific threats that the Executive Orders purported to address. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) The court determined that merely creating leverage does not meet the statute's \"deal with\" standard. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10)\n*   **Conflict with IEEPA's Intent:** The CIT stated that IEEPA was not intended to grant unfettered power to impose tariffs, and that Section 122 of IEEPA (allowing tariffs to be imposed to respond to balance of payments problems) is the only authorization to impose tariffs pursuant to the statute. [worldtradelaw](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-10)\n\n**Important Considerations:**\n\n*   **Stay Pending Appeal:** It's crucial to note that the Federal Circuit Court of Appeals granted a stay pending appeal, which means the IEEPA tariffs remain in effect while the appeal is considered. [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0) [ey](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-2) [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4) [hunton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-6)\n*   **Expedited Review:** The Federal Circuit is set to hear the cases en banc (by the full court) on an expedited basis, suggesting a fast-tracked decision on the merits. [cov](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-0)\n*   **Other Legal Authorities:** Even if the IEEPA tariffs are ultimately struck down, the President may attempt to use other legal authorities to impose similar tariffs, though these may come with limitations and potential for further litigation. [mofo](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-4)\n*   **Supreme Court:** Legal challenges to the tariffs may ultimately reach the Supreme Court. [grantthornton](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-9) [scotusblog](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/4-1)\n*   **Refunds:** The CIT's ruling declared the IEEPA tariffs illegal for all importers but did not explicitly order the government to issue refunds.
